Batavia All members of the executive committee of the Dutch East Indies Nationalist Party were arrested today on suspicion of plotting to disturb public order. The authorities are also conducting house-to-house searches for seditious documents. (Reuters, 25th)

Saito's Response to Questions in the House of Peers

Strict Control of Right-Wing Violent Actions

(Tokyo) The House of Peers Budget Committee convened at 10:00 AM on the 26th. Kobayashi Kiheiji of the Dowakai questioned Minister of Education Hatoyama regarding education issues. Subsequently, Matsumura Giichi questioned Prime Minister Saito about security matters. The Prime Minister responded, stating,

The government must strictly control violent behavior. While it is difficult to control the ideology of right-wing factions, their violence must be suppressed.

In response to a question from Sakamoto Toshiatsu, he replied,

The government has not yet decided whether to establish a new agency for fuel issues. As for establishing a national defense conference, the Resources Investigation Committee is currently investigating it.

Matsumura Giichi further questioned the Prime Minister, saying,

The Prime Minister says he will not control right-wing ideology, but among the right-wing are those who attempt to radically change the social structure. Will the government continue to allow this?

The Prime Minister replied,

It cannot be allowed.

Next, Baron Iwakura questioned,

The current Manchurian institutions are transitional, so talent and capital do not flow to Manchuria. The government has no fundamental investigation into Manchurian economic work. Under the current system, satisfactory development of Manchuria cannot be expected.

The Prime Minister replied,

Currently, due to the transitional period, affairs are being conducted with a tripartite system. The system will gradually change in the future. Next, Count Niara spoke about national ideology and then said,

We should make the world recognize "Manchukuo." To this end, please support the government's efforts to have "Manchukuo" participate in the Far Eastern Games.

Minister of Education Hatoyama replied,

The issue of "Manchukuo" participating in the Far Eastern Games has been agreed to by the Philippines. However, China has not recognized it. Efforts will be made in the future to have "Manchukuo" attend the Games.

Finally, after Matsumura's questioning, the meeting adjourned at 12:15 PM. (Jiji News Agency, 26th)

(Tokyo) At around 2:00 PM today, a large man suddenly broke into the Ministry of Education, threatening Minister of Education Hatoyama to resign. He was immediately arrested by the Kojimachi Police Station. Fortunately, Minister of Education Hatoyama was not injured in any way. The violent man's name is Moriyama Goro, 30 years old, and he is said to be a member of a right-leaning group. (Jiji News Agency, 26th)

Internal Strife Within the Seiyukai Subsides

Mochizuki's Resignation Scene Takes Effect

(Tokyo) Within the Seiyukai, there has always been opposition to President Suzuki and Minister of Education Hatoyama, especially the dissatisfaction of the Kuhara and Tokonami factions. Therefore, there were often secret struggles within the party, carrying out various maneuvers. When Mr. Tokonami's speech at the beginning of this session of the Diet was welcomed by the political world, the members of that faction took the opportunity to attempt a grand alliance, oppose President Suzuki, and plot to unite the members of the Sei, Min, and Koku Do three parties to form a "Unified Club" with Tokonami as chairman, beginning a non-partisan political movement. Within the Seiyukai, they were then divided into a grand alliance faction and its opposition. The struggle gradually intensified, and some members took advantage of this atmosphere to plan and create a fascist atmosphere, and there were those who attempted to create a Hiranuma Cabinet or a Yamamoto Cabinet. When Kazumi Okamoto exposed the disciplinary issues of Minister of Education Hatoyama and Minister of Railways Mitsuchi, this internal strife became more intense, leading to the danger of the Seiyukai splitting. Party elder Keisuke Mochizuki, who had previously been in contact with the Kuhara and Tokonami factions and expressed goodwill towards the grand alliance movement, suddenly declared that he would take full responsibility and proceed with resignation procedures. The Seiyukai was very embarrassed by Mochizuki's resignation, as he was an important figure in the party headquarters, and his resignation had a major impact on the political world. Executives and other important figures tried hard to persuade him to stay, and he then dispelled his intention to resign. At this point, the internal strife of the Seiyukai, apart from the issue of the reinstatement of party members Tsugumo and Nishikata, has reached a happy conclusion. The grand drama of Mochizuki's resignation has also come to an end. (Jiji News Agency, 26th)

Severe Wind and Snowstorm in America

Large Trees Uprooted, Injuries and Deaths Cause Concern

Plane Carrying Eight Passengers Crashes

(New York) The snow in New England has not yet melted, and a heavy snowstorm with severe winds has started again this afternoon. Large trees are uprooted, and houses are greatly damaged. All transportation is suspended, and residents of Long Island are worried about the interruption of food and fuel supplies. Today, Illinois had eight inches of snow, and West Virginia had sixteen inches. There are many deaths, but the exact number is unknown. A woman froze to death on a street in Philadelphia. Mississippi, Georgia, and Alabama experienced severe winds, resulting in eight deaths, twelve injuries, and significant property damage. A plane carrying eight passengers crashed on Friday after flying to Salt Lake City due to a snowstorm. Its whereabouts are unknown. Another plane is currently searching for it in the Wasatch Mountains, but it cannot be determined whether the plane is damaged. (Reuters, 25th)

(New York) Ice and snow have caused disasters in various places, followed by torrential rain. Mississippi, Alabama, and Georgia have been particularly severely affected. In Choctaw County, Mississippi, a couple and their four children were killed. In Clay County, Alabama, a black man and a woman died. Most were crushed to death by collapsed houses. There are about forty injured, and the material losses are enormous. More than fifty houses have been destroyed, and trees and utility poles have been blown down by the wind. Road traffic is blocked. In the central, western, and eastern United States, the wind and snow from Oklahoma and Nebraska have blown to the Atlantic coast and have not yet stopped. Four people have died, and vehicle traffic is almost completely stopped. The snow on the highways in central Illinois is 50 centimeters high. Heavy snow has fallen in major cities such as Chicago, Washington, and New York. The weather is extremely cold. The number of people who froze to death near New York has increased by two. Airmail in New York has been completely suspended, and other airlines have stopped carrying passengers. Private companies in New York have stopped transporting goods to various parts of the United States. A car overturned on a bridge in Sacramento, California, because the driver could not see the road in the heavy rain, resulting in the death of four passengers. In Caribou, Maine, a train derailed due to heavy snow, killing the engineer. The fireman jumped from the engine and saved his life. (Havas, 25th)

Soviet Authorities Dispatch Airplanes to Rescue

(Moscow) Many large ice floes in the Caspian Sea have broken, and the fishermen on the ice floes are drifting at sea, their whereabouts unknown. Their fate is of great concern. There are four hundred fishermen and one hundred and ninety horses, but food is scarce, and they may starve to death. The authorities have dispatched airplanes to search for the ice floes where the fishermen are located and drop medicine and food. At the same time, icebreakers have been dispatched to rescue them. Central Government Plans to Establish a Silver Price Research Association

Engaging Domestic Economic Experts

Researching the Issue of Stabilizing Silver Prices

(Nanjing) The central government believes that the US's issue of raising silver prices is of great importance and plans to order the Economic Council, the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, and other relevant departments to engage domestic economic experts to organize a Central Silver Price Research Association to study countermeasures. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Industry's Silver Price Issue Research Committee held its first meeting on the 26th to exchange views. Concrete results will be presented to the central government for reference. (Special Dispatch, 26th)

(Nanjing) Peng Xuepei, Director of the Executive Yuan's Political Affairs Department, said that the government had already begun researching the issue of the US raising silver prices before receiving a telegram from the Shanghai banking community, planning for a rainy day. Measures will be taken once the US implements its policy, but all methods, such as banning silver exports, are still under study.

(Nanjing) Economist Liu Zhendong said that the US's plan to raise silver prices has caused domestic panic, similar to the phenomenon of gold prices soaring and silver prices plummeting several years ago. However, the impact of cheap silver several years ago did not harm the country's wealth and purchasing power. Only international trade was disrupted due to different exchange rates. The US's current plan to raise silver prices aims to dump US goods on other countries, but this method will not last. If there is unlimited minting of silver coins, it will cause silver prices to fall. As a silver-using country, China is now in a passive position. The only way is to stabilize domestic currency prices, maintain commodity prices, and implement the collection of silver export taxes or a ban on exports. (China Central News Agency, 26th)

(Nanjing) Tang Chengbo, Chief Secretary of the Ministry of Industry, said that the Executive Yuan had already studied the issue of soaring silver prices before receiving a telegram from the Shanghai banking community. The Ministry will pay attention to the impact of high silver prices on industry. Minister Chen has also engaged experts to discuss fundamental and short-term solutions. The result of high silver prices will inevitably be lower commodity prices, and various industries will inevitably collapse. The financial community will also panic due to debt difficulties. Farmers will suffer quickly and obviously, and workers will suffer unemployment. The approval of the silver agreement has no absolute relationship with this issue. The fundamental purpose of the agreement is to reduce silver price fluctuations, not to raise silver prices. If the government believes it can approve it, it should attach reservations, stating that if there is a violation of the spirit of the agreement, seeking to raise silver prices, we have the right to act freely. Furthermore, the US's silver policy has not yet been clearly announced. If it proves to be actively raising silver prices, then the fundamental purpose of the agreement has been lost. The government may simply not approve it for this reason. (China Central News Agency, 26th)

Reports from Central Government and National Government Memorial Weeks

Tan Zhen: National Salvation Issues

Zeng Kuangqing: Party Affairs in Sichuan Province

(Nanjing) The Central Government held its 119th Memorial Week on the 26th. Ju Zheng, Chen Lifu, Li Zonghuang, Fang Juehui, Hong Ludong, Li Ciwen, Zeng Kuangqing, Miao Peicheng, Xie Zuomin, Zheng Zhannan, and about 500 staff members attended. Ju Zheng chaired the meeting. Zeng Kuangqing reported, saying that the Party affairs in Sichuan Province were unable to fulfill the responsibility of leading the people because the past leaders had extremely inconsistent opinions and frequent disputes. Since the Central Government sent him as a special commissioner for Party affairs to Sichuan to preside over the matter, he repeatedly explained the importance of sincerity to his comrades in order to eliminate differences and unite sincerely to achieve the effect of unifying Party affairs. Currently, the former leaders are all working hard under the leadership of the special commissioner, and the results are good. In addition, the military in Sichuan Province used to have soldiers who each possessed huge armies and competed for defense areas, resulting in the number of troops in the province reaching more than 500,000. The disputes and looting led to a daily increase in exorbitant taxes, which the people could not bear. Since the communist bandit Xu Xiangqian infiltrated Sichuan and disturbed the Tongba and Sui areas, the military in Sichuan Province has been deeply stimulated and can eliminate the old conflicting opinions and unanimously advance to suppress the red bandits. The local defense militias have also realized that the bandit threat is worrying and do not compromise on territory, cooperating in eliminating bandits. Future success will surely be achieved. Sichuan Province is a wealthy area. When foreign troubles are becoming increasingly urgent and national defense is not solid, the nation's economic center of gravity may be shifted from Shanghai and Tianjin to Sichuan Province, to serve as the basis for long-term resistance to prolong the survival of the nation. He hoped that all comrades would pay attention to it. The meeting adjourned after 10:00 AM. (China Central News Agency, 26th)

(Nanjing) The National Government held a memorial week at 10:00 AM on the 26th. Zhang Ji, Tan Zhen, Niu Yongjian, Zhu Peide, Chen Shaokuan, He Yaozu, Chen Xunyong, Wang Yongbin, Chen Shuren, Lin Chao, Wei Huai, and more than 400 National Government staff attended. Chairman Lin led the ceremony. Tan Zhen's report, entitled The Fundamental Problems of Saving China, first described the decline of our nation, the decline of its spirit, and the increasing disaster and famine, which have led to an increase in the death rate. The current population is less than 400 million. Therefore, saving the country today means saving the nation and improving the race. He then said that the crisis of 1936 is imminent. Observing the governance of Mussolini and the policies of Hitler after taking power in Germany, they all focus on encouraging reproduction and promoting eugenics. With the danger urgent, we should exhaust the power of the government and society to engage in the plan to preserve the race and save the country, learn from the legacy of King Yue's ten years of growth and ten years of teaching, to build a young China and avoid elimination. (China Central News Agency, 26th)

Regarding the relief measures, it is said that an additional three and a half jin of un-taxed brine waste is added for every hundred jin of salt. That is, for every 103.5 jin of salt, tax is collected based on 100 jin. Although the tax burden on salt merchants is heavier than before, it is still bearable. One Coin of Parisian Citizens' Riot (Paris Aviation Correspondence)

Demonstrators Break Through Police Line

Prosperous City Streets Become a Slaughterhouse

The tranquility of Paris, its prosperity, and its comfort are universally known and praised. Although recent political unrest has been unpleasant, the changes in the cabinet have been limited to the replacement of government officials and have not had a major impact on France's future or its foreign policy. However, a relatively serious event has recently occurred.

Photo Eight of the Organization of a Puppet Government in Southern Xinjiang

This photo shows the leaders of the bandits who were in charge of military affairs during the Kashgar rebellion.

1. Bandit Leader of the Bu (Unknown Name)

2. Yuman, Younger Brother of Bu Bandit Usman, Bandit Leader. Contacted Hui Bandits on August 16th and was Killed by Them

3. Bu Bandit Leader, Wo Nuosi, Now Promoted to Division Commander

4. Hui Bandit Leader, Ma (Unknown Name), Rumored to be Killed by Chan Bandits

5. Hui Bandit Leader, Ma Zhancang

6. Chan Bandit Leader, Temuer

7. Hui Bandit Brigade Commander, Ke Mazi (From Yanqi)

8. Ai Men Danbaike Aji (From Afghanistan)

9. Ke Qi Ke Bandit Leader

The People Standing Behind are all Ma Zhancang's Guards

It is the imbalance of the budget and the inadequacy of national treasury revenue that has aroused extreme resentment among the general public. From the extreme right to the extreme left, all are filled with resentment and want to break the current situation and create a new one, but it is always not easy to get an opportunity to incite the masses. This time, it happened to encounter the pawnshop operated by the Bayonne Municipal Government issuing improper municipal bonds, which further aroused public resentment and involved members of the Xu Dan cabinet and the former police chief. Thus, the citizens unanimously resented and, upon the call of the right-wing, formed a majority of the masses. This matter began in late January and became more active in early February. Although the French government tried to maintain calm, the Royalist Party, the Socialist Party, and the Communist Party all worked hard to instigate. On the afternoon of February 6, a major riot broke out. Demonstrators, holding stones and wooden sticks, broke through the police line on the Concorde Bridge and surrounded the parliament. The number of people and police officers injured at that time, according to unofficial investigations, was more than four hundred, and the number of deaths was twelve. It has not subsided until this morning.

Now, let's put aside the situation of the riot for the time being and report the process that led to this riot. What exactly is the illegal event of the Bayonne Municipal Pawnshop? It is still not easy for us to make an immediate judgment, but it has been investigated by the police department and the Ministry of Interior. It is said that the number of these illegal bonds issued is about four to five hundred million francs. The issuer of these bonds is the head of the pawnshop, Texie. Under normal circumstances, to issue bonds, one must register with the government. These four to five hundred million francs of bonds were all issued by Texie privately, without government registration.

The process of its discovery was that one of the investors, the Erpen Insurance Company, requested repayment of the matured bonds, but received no response. Therefore, it was discovered by the government immediately. Texie was arrested immediately. The time of his arrest was December 25th of last year. After several studies, it was learned that the initiator of this illegal event was not Texie, but another reputable person. This person is called Alexandre Stavisky.

Stavisky is the central figure who aroused this riot. Perhaps people in our country do not understand him very well, so I will give a brief introduction. Stavisky is a Russian-Greek. His father was a dentist. He only entered French citizenship before the war. He is a very intelligent person. He is a repeat offender of fraud and scams. In France, he became famous in 1926. His main business is as a business initiator. Real estate companies, gemstone companies, elevated railways, subway roads, etc. are all his targets. In 1926, the reason why he suddenly became famous was the same as this time, it was the issuance of illegal bonds by the Alain Public Pawnshop, but because the evidence was insufficient, he was released. Therefore, the general French society knows that he is a great swindler. From that time on, the business he initiated expanded to the international level, especially in Hungary, he bought frozen bonds to use as a tool to manipulate the market. In Paris, he operated several theaters, and the "Vioronto" new newspaper was under his control. His speculation is very rich. When gambling, he does not change his face even if he spends millions. The big fraud case of 1926 gradually disappeared into the darkness, and he became prosperous day by day in inverse proportion to the darkness. His reputation was getting better and better day by day. His footprints were everywhere in the Parisian social circles.

In this case of illegal issuance of bonds, after Texie was arrested, he was also summoned for questioning, but he was released again due to insufficient evidence. However, since the day he was released, his shadow has no longer been seen in the Parisian social scene. This has caused the Parisian citizens, especially the masses under the right-wing parties, to become more suspicious. They thought that he was the initiator of the Bayonne Municipal Pawnshop, and Texie was his friend, so he was the core figure in the scam. There is no need for any more evidence. This problem has gradually become serious, even affecting the Xu Dan cabinet. Unexpectedly, the news of Stavisky's suicide was announced on January 9, and the problem was temporarily simplified, and the Xu Dan cabinet was able to survive. However, Stavisky's suicide is still hidden in the dark curtain. The right-wing "Paris Echo" and the socialist newspaper "People" all expressed suspicion and attacked the government. Xu Dan finally could not support it. It is also a question what Daradi will do after he comes to power. The masses in Paris are singing the Marseillaise everywhere, chanting the slogans "Down with the government" and "Put the former police chief Shabai in jail." Demonstrations and demonstrations are all over Paris. Yesterday's prosperity suddenly turned into terror today. What will happen in the future, I really dare not judge lightly. (Morning of February 7, 1934, in Paris)

Difficulties After the Re-taking of Yuguan

Puppet Organs Show No Intention of Withdrawing

Our Police Still Wear Puppet Uniforms

Japan Refuses to Return the Sixteen Passes of the Great Wall

Tianjin Correspondence, It has been half a month since Yuguan was retaken on February 10. Tao Shangming and Yuan Tai, the magistrate of Linyu County, have come to Tianjin to report. According to them, after retaking Yuguan, the political situation is good, and the officers of both sides are getting along well, but the various puppet organs have not yet withdrawn. After Tao Shangming visited Yu Xuezhong, the Chairman of Hebei Province, in Tianjin, he went to Pingjin to request instructions from the Military Branch Council and the Political Affairs Committee on the re-taking of the various passes of the Great Wall. He can return to Tianjin and then return to Yuguan in the next few days. It is reported that Tao and others are conducting negotiations with the Japanese on two matters: one is the withdrawal of the puppet Japanese organs, and the other is the re-taking of the various passes of the Great Wall. The puppet Japanese organs that have not yet withdrawn at present include the Japanese Military Police Detachment, the Headquarters of the Kawakai Garrison, the Japanese Police Station, the Puppet Border Police Force, the Suixing Tax Branch, the Puppet Border Passport Verification Office, the Puppet Shanhaiguan Telegraph Bureau, the Puppet Shanhaiguan Post Office, and the Puppet Shanhaiguan Customs, and more than ten other organs. Among them, the Puppet Post Office occupies our Telegraph Bureau's building, making it impossible for our Telegraph Bureau to resume operations. The Puppet Border Police Force exercises its authority at the station, and there are also many conflicts with the authority of our Beining Railway and the Shanhaiguan Special Public Security Bureau. Therefore, Tao Shangming will ask the Japanese representative Igi to demand that they must withdraw. After the establishment of our Special Public Security Bureau, the police have been staffed to one hundred and twenty, including fifty recruited during the maintenance association era. Within one to two months, another eighty will be recruited, for a total of two hundred. Previously, the Japanese did not allow our police to carry firearms, but after Su Yuqi repeatedly negotiated with the Japanese, they allowed fifty of them to be equipped with handguns and short knives, but absolutely did not allow them to be equipped with rifles. Su believed that only fifty out of two hundred police officers were allowed to be equipped with guns and knives, the number was too small to maintain ground security, and he has asked Tao Shangming to relay to the Japanese side that it is still necessary for each person to be equipped with guns and knives. Due to financial reasons, the police uniforms of the police officers under the management of the maintenance association still wear the puppet national police uniforms. They must be changed when wearing jackets after the spring warms up. At present, only the five-pointed star emblem of the puppet country on the hat flower has been removed and replaced with our Jiahe. The general members of the local maintenance association have always opposed the authorities taking over the regime. Because of this, they must nag the Japanese in front of the Japanese, attacking Su Yuqi and Yuan Tai, and plan to move to revive the puppet organization. Some Japanese ruffians and the Japanese military police team enter and exit the public security bureau and the county government all day long, investigating our measures. Although Su Yuqi and Yuan Tai are overwhelmed by it, they have no way to refuse. Japan has some regrets about handing over a part of the regime. The puppet Japanese organs in Yuguan have expressed that they will never withdraw. It is also difficult to negotiate how Tao Shangming will negotiate in the future. Within the Luanyu Administrative Region, the sixteen Great Wall passes of all sizes designated by the Political Consolidation Council to be taken over by Tao Shangming include Panjiakou, Lengkou, Jiunmenkou, Yiyuan Kou, and Jielingkou. At these five major passes, the Japanese built barracks last year. Recently, they informally expressed to our side that the bandit atmosphere on the Great Wall Line is not peaceful. In order to ensure the safety of Manchuria, they will not return it for the time being. The small passes can be taken over by our side. In fact, no Japanese troops are stationed at the small passes, and there is no need to take them over. In order to prevent Japanese puppet troops from crossing the border and invading, our side must reorganize the defenses of the small passes, send armed security teams, and set up long-distance military telephones. However, this seems unnecessary at this time, and I am afraid that the Japanese side may not agree to our reorganization. Therefore, Tao Shangming's purpose in going to Yuguan this time is still to negotiate for the simultaneous takeover on the 16th. (24th)

Slight Changes in the Guangdong Army's Fujian-Jiangxi Front

Continued Construction of Defense Works in Southern Fujian

Sichuan-Kang Survey Group Inspects Guankou Irrigation Works

丨The Whole Group Departs from Chengdu in Two Routes丨

The Shanghai reporters of the Sichuan-Kang Survey Group arrived in Chengdu on February 9. They originally intended to complete preparations within three days and then depart in two routes, one going to western Sichuan and the other to northern Sichuan, to make every effort to conduct survey work. However, Sichuan still observes the customs of the old lunar year. All industries are closed for the first five days of the new year, and there is no way to arrange for porters and food needed for the journey. Moreover, the generals of various fronts happened to gather in Chengdu to hold an anti-bandit meeting to discuss the second phase of the anti-bandit plan. Therefore, the reporter group decided to stay in Chengdu temporarily and take this opportunity to interview the generals once. The itinerary was also slightly delayed.

Chengdu Dam (the Main Hub of Various Rivers) (Photo by Wang Zhenhuan)

On February 12, they interviewed Liu Xiang, Deng Xihou, Tian Songyao, and Yang Sen. All four said that the most important task at present is to suppress the bandits, and they must devote all their efforts to complete it in the shortest possible time. Since the recovery of Xuanhan, Dazhou, Yingshan, Yilong, and other counties, the military cooperation has been very effective, and it is quite possible to completely eliminate the bandits within a month. After the completion of the bandit suppression, the second step is the issue of post-war reconstruction. This issue includes the method of demobilizing troops throughout Sichuan and the method of unifying administration and finance. The purpose is to separate military power from political power so that finances can be balanced. The third step is to engage in development, that is, to pay attention to industrial construction, transportation, and so on.

On the 13th, they visited West China University. The university's dental department is the most complete. It is said to be the first in our country and the third in the world. The medical department and the liberal arts and science departments are all well-equipped. The entire school covers an area of more than a thousand acres, and the buildings are magnificent and the environment is extremely quiet. The museum houses a very rich collection of ancient artifacts and Xikang materials. There are 451 students in the university department, most of whom are able to concentrate on their studies. The founder of the school was an American named Bi Qi. He came to Sichuan alone, saw the good situation in Chengdu, and was determined to establish a university here. After more than twenty years of continuous efforts, fundraising, and planning, he finally achieved what he has today.

On the 15th, they went to Guankou to observe the irrigation works. In advance, Tong Zhiquan, who had served as the magistrate in charge of water conservancy, provided drawings, and Zhou Yuru, the current magistrate, explained them in detail, so they were able to understand the general situation. Guankou is located 140 miles northwest of Chengdu. The two sources of the Min River converge here and flow down into the Chengdu Dam. The Chengdu Dam is a very large plain with fourteen counties, millions of acres of farmland, fertile land, and crisscrossing ditches. There are nine major rivers, all of which branch out from Guankou. Therefore, Guankou is the main hub of all the rivers in the Chengdu Dam, and the drought and floods in the entire area are controlled by Guankou. During the Qin Dynasty, floods were rampant. Li Bing, the governor of Shu, and his son Erlang built the Lidui, Baopingkou, and Yu Zui Ma Cuo projects to ensure that the water flowing down had a fixed amount and could be controlled. During floods, water can be diverted into the outer river, and during droughts, it can all be diverted into the inner river. They also made rulers for measurement and compiled songs to facilitate memory. For thousands of years, water managers have followed them. Chengdu has no floods, and the people of Shu respect them as the Lord of Sichuan. The greatness of their achievements can be imagined. There is a temple there that enshrines the statues of Li Bing and his son. Local people are very respectful and remember their contributions to people's livelihood. On August 25 last year, the geological layer collapsed 400 miles from Guankou in the upper reaches of the Min River, causing landslides and water blockage, which suddenly reduced the amount of water downstream. According to investigations, the accumulated water has now frozen, and the earthquake has not yet stopped. There is fear that the ice will melt this spring and the old projects may not be able to withstand the floods. Therefore, measures have been taken to dredge the river so that it can continue to flow down. According to electrical engineer Luo Jingzhan, the water power of Guankou is extremely large and can generate more than 100,000 horsepower of electricity, which requires a capital of 40 to 50 million yuan. Only by experienced engineers can a huge project be successful. However, there are no factories nearby that can consume so much electricity, so it cannot be held until the industry has developed to a considerable level. At this time, we can only sit and watch the stream of water and waste its capacity.

After many days of contact, the country decided to depart in two routes. The first route goes to northern Sichuan, passes through the rear of the various armies, and returns to Chongqing. The second route goes to western Sichuan, passes through Ya'an to reach Daqianlu, and returns east along the Yangtze River, meeting the first route in Chongqing. Both routes take about a month and a half. In addition to production and construction, and social conditions, the first route will also observe the conditions of the bandit areas, and the second route will pay attention to border defense issues. Among the seven members of the group, Zhang Xianmei, Chen Youqin, and Liu Sida will take the first route, and Lu Yitang, Hui Ping, Su Dezheng, and Wang Zhenhuan will take the second route. The departure date is February 19. (Published from Chengdu on the 18th by Lixing)

Verdict Announced on Appeal of Suzhou Car Accident Case

Shi Guobin, a lieutenant colonel translator at the Nanjing Army University, was struck and killed by a car driven by Chen Jinsheng, the driver of Lu Tongcun, the Shanghai Bank district manager, on December 19 last year. Chen Jinsheng, the driver who caused the accident, was arrested by the police and sent to court, which sentenced him to two years in prison for causing death by negligence. The accompanying private lawsuit sought joint compensation for losses of 99,840 yuan. The defendants Lu Tongcun and Chen Jinsheng refused to accept the verdict and appealed to the Jiangsu High Court. The Second Division concluded the trial and the presiding judge Wu executed the verdict yesterday (26th) at 3:00 PM. The main text stated that Chen Jinsheng's appeal was rejected and the original sentence was maintained. The original verdict of the accompanying private lawsuit was revoked and changed to a fine of 40,000 yuan.

Xu Yabo's Appeal Ruled Not Guilty

Xu Yabo, the former director of the First District of Jiangsu Water Police, was falsely accused of jointly committing robbery and sentenced to seven years in prison in the first instance. Xu refused to accept the verdict and appealed to the Jiangsu High Court, which declared him not guilty. The prosecuting attorney refused to accept the verdict and appealed to the Supreme Court. As a result, the case was sent back to the Jiangsu High Court for retrial. Yesterday (26th), Xu Yabo was declared not guilty.

Wuxi and Bengbu Grain Merchants Oppose Increasing Commission

The Wuxi Rice, Bean and Miscellaneous Grains Guild, previously due to low grain prices and sluggish market conditions that led to insufficient expenditure, jointly with the Wujin Guild, changed the original 99-to-1 exchange rate to 98.4. This was met with strong opposition from the Bengbu Grain Merchants' Guild, Transportation Guild, and Jiangsu Grain Merchants' Guild in Bengbu. Therefore, a joint meeting was convened on the previous day at Jiyu Hall, gathering the rice and bean merchants of Wuxi and Wujin counties to discuss countermeasures. It was decided that, according to Bengbu's precedent, a commission of one dime would be deducted for each dan (unit of weight) of miscellaneous grains priced at ten yuan or less. If the price per dan was more than ten yuan, the original 99-to-1 exchange rate would still be used. For example, if the price of soybeans was five yuan, deducting a commission of one dime would result in an exchange rate of 98. Currently, there is no possibility of miscellaneous grains rising to ten yuan per dan. If Bengbu grain merchants come to Wuxi to negotiate, this is how they will respond. After the meeting, Bengbu grain merchants came to Wuxi that evening and, upon learning the above information, found a significant difference in opinions between the two sides. They returned to Bengbu yesterday and will need to collectively discuss the matter within the three groups before coming to Wuxi again for negotiations.

Ring Leader of the Bandit Gang in Changzhou Arrested for Crimes Committed in Suzhou

The Wuyi County Government recently received a tip that a person nicknamed "Stone" Yang Rongsheng, from Zhenglu Bridge Town in the northern part of the county, had gathered more than ten people to commit robbery at Wudong Bridge outside Qimen in Suzhou during the eighth month of last year. The county had already arrested a suspect in the case, Zhong Rongbing. However, Yang Rongsheng fled back to Changzhou and hid in Xixiashu Town. For prudence's sake, County Magistrate Cai specifically wrote to the Wuxian County Government to inquire whether the robbery case had occurred and whether the suspect, Zhong Rongbing, had identified Yang Rongsheng as the ringleader. A reply was received confirming that the situation was accurate. A detective team was secretly dispatched to Xixiashu to investigate and arrest Yang. They learned that Yang had escaped back to his home. They then went to Zhengliu Bridge to investigate and, at night, surrounded and arrested him at his home. On the 24th, he was sent to the county for interrogation. On the 25th, County Magistrate Cai sent a dispatch to the Wuxian County Government, requesting them to send police officers to Changzhou to escort him back for trial.

Zhenjiang Organizes a Association to Promote National Products

The Jiangsu Provincial Capital Citizens' National Products Promotion Association held an inaugural meeting of initiators yesterday at Wujiaxiang, with over forty people attending. The Provincial Party Headquarters specially sent Wang Lu to attend and provide guidance. After the meeting opened, the report was presented first, followed by a discussion of the draft charter and funding issues. All matters were handed over to the preparatory committee. Finally, all the initiators voted to elect seven people as members of the preparatory committee. It is reported that the first preparatory meeting is scheduled for March 1st.

Large Cannonball Found on the Riverside

After the river tide receded yesterday, a large cannonball was suddenly discovered on the river beach of the local China Merchants Wharf. It weighed about seventy or eighty catties. Subsequently, a cleaner from the Fourth Precinct noticed it and carried it to the precinct.

Only Two Money Exchange Shops Remaining in Xiannv Town, Yangzhou

Xiannv Town, located in the fourth district of the county, is a bustling market town in the eastern countryside. Since the failure of the money and lumber industries, the market has also declined. During the lunar new year, Yuansheng and Fukang both closed down. This spring, Runkan money shop also went bankrupt. Currently, only two money shops remain in the town: Zhentai and Hengtai.

Bandit Case Solved in Jinsha, Nantong

A bandit robbery occurred in Jinsha on the morning of the 14th. Yuchang Lumber Company and other households suffered significant losses. The police and local militia have now solved the case and arrested the bandits Xu Dongkou, Zhang Jin, Xing Jiaru, and Qian Qiao. They were sent to the county government for interrogation on the 24th.

Disbandment of Temporarily Recruited Soldiers from the Defense Regiment

The Nantong County Defense Regiment has reorganized its headquarters. County Magistrate Cheng Yuyan is the general commander, and Peng Longxiang is the deputy commander. All the temporary soldiers recruited by the regiments in various districts of the county have been dismissed, and new soldiers will be drafted and organized separately.

Special Feature

Impressions of an Economic Survey in Guangxi Province (3) by Qian Jiaxun

After arriving in Wuzhou, we stayed at the Danan Hotel and decided to hire a car to go to Yongning (Nanning) early the next morning. It is over a thousand li from Wuzhou to Yongning. Both water and land routes are available. The water route goes through Pingnan, Guiping, Guixian, Hengxian, Yongchun, etc. Taking the Yongwu Express Ferry takes about three days. The land route is the highway, going through Rongxian, Beiliu, Yulin, Guixian, Binyang, etc. The fastest it takes by car is one day, but you have to depart at 4:00 am and arrive at 8:00 or 9:00 pm. Otherwise, it takes two days, staying overnight in Guixian. We wanted to arrive in one day. We carried small luggage ourselves, and the big luggage was transported by ship. That afternoon, Deputy Commander Bai and Military Commander Xia sent us a note to invite us and Dr. Shi from the German medical team to dinner at Qunle Restaurant. At one o'clock, Deputy Officer Qiu picked us up in a car and first drove us around Wuzhou City, then took us to Zhongshan Park to visit the Zhongshan Memorial Hall. The hall is on the top of the mountain. Overlooking Wuzhou City, we saw the Fu River and the Great River converging here. The water was one green and one yellow, clearly demarcated, as if enveloping the whole city. The people of Guangxi also call it the Yuan River, truly a beautiful sight. After visiting the Zhongshan Memorial Hall, we went to the restaurant. At that time, Deputy Commander Bai was still in Yongning, and Military Commander Xia had not arrived either. The company included various chiefs of staff, division chiefs, and the chief of the Public Security Bureau. We took the opportunity to tell them that we might need to come to Wuzhou again for an economic survey and would need their help in many areas. After leaving Qunle Restaurant, reporters from the Wuzhou Republic Daily and Dagong Daily (not the Dagong Daily of Tianjin) came to visit and we spoke for half an hour. After the reporters left, we covered ourselves and went to sleep, preparing for the long journey the next day.

The next morning at four o'clock, Deputy Officer Qiu woke us up. After we washed and tidied up, we made a few minor adjustments to our scattered belongings and strolled out of the hotel to the ferry pier. At this time, the morning light was faint, and the streets were pitch black with not a soul in sight. A police officers were dozing by the side of the road. After arriving at the ferry pier, we had to sit in a "foreign paddle boat" for more than an hour to get to the Rongxu bus station (the Yongwu Highway only goes to Rongxu in Wuzhou). By the time we arrived, it was daylight. The four of us got into the hired car, and the car sped off. Although this section of the highway was relatively smooth, the speed of the car was so fast that it was very bumpy. We passed through Cenxi, Rongxian, Beiliu, Yulin, Xingye, etc. Along the way, there were sudden downpours and scorching sun, as if traveling in the desert. At the same time, the differences in climate in various places could be seen in the crops. Some rice was heavy with grain, nearing harvest time, while in other places, the rice was only a foot long. After passing Guixian, the mountains were somewhat different from what we were used to seeing. The peaks of the rocky mountains were towering, exquisite, and verdant. We were like Grandma Liu entering the Grand View Garden for the first time, praising without ceasing, unable to take it all in, almost forgetting that we were on a journey. It was not until later, when we arrived at Yangshuo and Guilin and saw the bizarre shapes of the hills, that we realized that what we had seen today was only the dregs of the Guangxi landscape.

Our car did not arrive in Nanning until 9:00 pm. After this sixteen-hour ordeal, coupled with the occasional rain and sunshine and the unpredictable cold and heat, not only was my body exhausted to the extreme, but I also caught a cold. After taking two aspirin tablets, I covered myself and went to sleep. The next morning, we went to the provincial government to pay our respects to Mr. Huang Xuchu, the chairman of the provincial government. Mr. Huang was taciturn, a man of great cultivation and decisiveness. We briefly reported on our journey. We originally intended to conduct an in-depth study of Guangxi's economic problems in Nanning based on existing materials before making plans for a field economic survey, so as to avoid the suspicion of armchair theorizing. Now, we were very willing to hear the opinions of their top leaders on Guangxi's economic construction. Mr. Huang's attitude was sincere and humble. He first expressed his warm welcome to our visit. Regarding the issue of Guangxi's economic construction, he said that he was completely ignorant and hoped that we economic experts would give him guidance. He then asked Mr. Yang Chuo'an, the director of the Bureau of Statistics, to be responsible for entertaining us, because the Bureau of Statistics had many ready-made books and statistical data. So we stayed at the Guangxi Bureau of Statistics.

Local News

Chinese and Foreign Representatives Held a Memorial Service for the King of Belgium at the Church Yesterday

Personally Hosted by the Belgian Envoy, Ji Youmu

Mayor Wu and Others Attended to Pay Respects

The Belgian Envoy Will Hold the Same Ceremony in Beijing Tonight

After the death of King Albert I of Belgium, the world sympathized and mourned. In addition to flying flags at half-mast for three days, yesterday afternoon the Belgian Envoy Ji Youmu, along with the Belgian Consul General and others, hosted a memorial service at St. Joseph's Church, inviting dignitaries from Chinese and foreign communities to pray for the King of Belgium. Song Ziwen, Wu Tiecheng, and others attended in person. The Belgian Envoy is scheduled to take the night train to Beijing tonight to host the same memorial service for Chinese and foreign representatives in the capital tomorrow. Details are provided below:

Attendees

Yesterday afternoon, many Chinese and foreign guests were invited to participate in the ceremony at St. Joseph's Church on Tianzhu Church Street. Those present included Song Ziwen, Standing Committee Member of the National Economic Council; Wu Tiecheng, Mayor of Shanghai; Chu Minyi, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan; Wang Jingqi, former Chinese Envoy to Belgium; Yu Ming, Director of the External Affairs Office; Wang Shouting, Commander of the Naval Training Squadron; Staff Officer Li Baoqi; Adjutant Zeng Guoqi; Yang Guangxun, Member of the National Economic Council; Zhao Tiezhang, Section Chief of the External Affairs Office; Tang Shixuan, Secretary of the Municipal Government; Geng Jiaji; Tang Haian, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs; and Lu Fei Bohong, among others. From the foreign community, there were Czech Envoy Fei Zhier; Russian Ambassador Bogomolov; Italian Envoy Boscali; Polish Envoy Weidengtao; Japanese Envoy Arima Akira; British Chargé d'Affaires Erringland; Swiss Chargé d'Affaires La Tai; Swedish Chargé d'Affaires Linquist; Norwegian Chargé d'Affaires Or; Chilean Chargé d'Affaires Sima Shi; Chief Tax Commissioner Merlo and; Tax Commissioner Claudius; Advisor Ba Du; Corps of Consuls Leader Ke Yinhan; Secretary-General Lang Ge; British Consul White Lee Nan; Japanese Consul Ishisa; French Consul Mei Li'ai; German Consul Bai Rende; Portuguese Consul Silva; British Naval Attaché Jark; American Military Attaché Baomeng; Commander of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps Gorahan; French Military Attaché Lai Man; Italian Military Attaché Kangsaranuo; Representative of the US Warship Hanson; Chief French Inspector La Bang; Deputy Director-General of the French Municipal Council; Italian Aviation Military Attaché Lao De; Director-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council Bell; Director Harris; Major General MacNoughton Belgian Priests Pray in Front of the Casket (Ye Changlie Photo)

; Macy; Yu Qiaqing; and the heads of the Engineering Department, Finance Department, Health Department, and Police Department of the Public Concession; as well as representatives from the Russian Association, the Sino-Belgian Friendship Association, the Italian Veterans Association, the French Chamber of Commerce, and other groups, totaling over five hundred people.

Wreath Donations

Among those who donated wreaths at the memorial service yesterday were Mayor Wu, Song Ziwen, Chu Minyi, and Yu Ming, as well as the Belgian Overseas Chinese Association, the British Chamber of Commerce, the British Overseas Chinese Association, and the Italian Fascist Association, all of whom laid wreaths before the spirit.

Interior and Exterior Arrangements

Inside the venue, which was St. Joseph's Church, a Belgian flag was hung high, with a crown above it and four black ribbons tied to the four pillars below the crown. The spirit and the area around the crucifix were decorated with wreaths sent by various circles. White candles were lit on the platforms on both sides. Mayor Wu's Wreath (Daily News Photo)

On the left side was the place for playing music, reciting the Bible, and the presiding priest. Outside the church courtyard, armed French Concession police and French sailors lined up in two rows on the left and right, paying respects to all the important Chinese and foreign figures entering and exiting the venue. Outside the gate, along Tianzhu Church Street and Gongguan Road, French Concession police officers and detectives were dispatched to direct traffic.

Prayer and Expression of Sentiment

At 11:20 am, the important Chinese and foreign figures arrived at the venue one after another. They were personally greeted by Belgian Envoy Ji Youmu and Belgian Consul General Dai Erfu. At 11:30 am, the bell was rung, and the Belgian Envoy followed the Abbot of Pu'ai Church into the venue to pay respects, standing up to read the Bible and sing hymns to pray for the King of Belgium. After several minutes of silence, they stood up again and paid respects to the King of Belgium and the Belgian flag. Military attachés from various countries who were wearing swords also raised their swords in salute. Then, the piano was played, and poems were recited for about an hour until 12:30 pm. The Belgian Envoy then went to the church door to shake hands with the representatives from all walks of life to express his gratitude. At the same time, sailors and police officers on both sides also raised their guns in salute. The ceremony ended at 12:40 pm.

Belgian Envoy Ji Youmu (center) posing for a photo leaving the church (Ye Changlie Photo)

Belgian Envoy Enters Beijing

Because the memorial service in the capital is scheduled to be held tomorrow noon, the Belgian Envoy sent his secretary, Mr. Meiyusi, to Beijing on the Beijing-Shanghai night train last night to make preparations. He himself is scheduled to take the Beijing-Shanghai night train with Belgian Consul General Dai Erfu and Vice Consul Dai Lihai tonight to personally host the same memorial service for Chinese and foreign representatives in Beijing tomorrow noon.

Newly Appointed British Envoy to China, Sir Odo Russell, Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning

Scheduled to Meet with the National Government Authorities in Beijing on the Second of Next Month

Will Present Credentials Next Week and Then Head North to Peiping

The British Chamber of Commerce and the United China Association Will Hold a Banquet Next Week

Sir Odo Russell, the newly appointed British Envoy to China, arrived in Shanghai on the British company liner "Chitral" to take up his new post with his wife and daughter. The representatives of the local Chinese and foreign communities boarded the ship to welcome him. The British Envoy disembarked at 9:15 and went directly to the British Consulate General for a short rest before checking into the Cathay Hotel. He is scheduled to go to Beijing on the 2nd and present his credentials next week. The details are as follows:

Arrival Situation

The "Chitral" entered Songkou at 6:20 yesterday morning and arrived at the Gonghexing Wharf at 7:30. The British Envoy had decided to disembark at 9:15, so he had breakfast on board. He then gathered with the welcoming personnel on board for a chat. At 9:15, led by the British Chargé d'Affaires to China, Erringland, and others, they disembarked and took cars to the British Consulate General on the Garden Bridge for a rest. Security was extremely tight along the way. Inside the consulate general, the British Shanghai Marine Corps and the military band were standing to welcome him. When the car carrying the British Envoy turned from the Garden Bridge into the gate of the consulate, the military music played in unison, and the soldiers raised their guns in salute. The British Envoy walked into the consulate in the sound of the beautiful military music to rest, and then checked into the Cathay Hotel.

Welcoming Personnel

Those who went to the pier to welcome him yesterday morning included Geng Jiaji, the representative of Mayor Wu; Yu Ming, the Director of the External Affairs Office; Xie Fusheng, the representative of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; Erringland, the British Chargé d'Affaires, and his secretary Eddington; British Consul-General in Shanghai, White Lee Nan; Consul Blackpon; Hallman, the First Secretary of the Embassy; William Wylly, Aviation Military Attaché; Justice Musu of the British Assessor's Office; Military Attaché Weir Lock; Marshal, the President of the British Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai, and dozens of others.

The Demeanor of the British Envoy

In addition to his wife and three daughters, there were also two attendants on the same ship with the British Envoy. As for Mr. Tai Qimen, the Chinese Secretary of the British Embassy, he had gone to Hong Kong a few days ago to represent the Chargé d'Affaires to welcome him and also arrived in Shanghai on the ship yesterday morning. In addition, Sir Teichman, the former Counselor of the British Embassy, returned to Hong Kong a few days ago after returning to the UK with the former British Envoy Lampson last year. This time he arrived in Shanghai on the same ship as the new Envoy. The British Envoy is about forty years old, with a light yellow beard, a tall and slender body, and bright and amiable eyes. Although Sir Odo has come to China for the first time, he has a very good understanding of the situation in the East.

Declining Social Engagements

Because the British Envoy is in the mourning period for King Albert I of Belgium, he has decided to decline all outside banquets. Therefore, the banquet set by Mayor Wu Tiecheng and others has now been canceled. However, the joint banquet of the British Chamber of Commerce and the United China Association in the city tomorrow night has been specially approved by the British Foreign Office. Because this banquet is an opportunity for the British Envoy to exchange views with the leaders of the British community, it will not be postponed. It is also heard that the Municipal Chamber of Commerce is also planning to hold a dinner party, and Xie Fusheng has gone to inquire whether it can be approved. The reply has not yet been received. Sir Odo is scheduled to go to Beijing on the 2nd and present his credentials in the middle of next week, and then go north to Peiping.

Mourning King of Belgium

After arriving at the Consulate General at 9:15, the British Envoy discussed the situation of the journey with Chargé d'Affaires Erringland. At 11:30, he drove to Tianzhu Church Street with Erringland and Consul-General White Lee Nan to participate in the ceremony to mourn the former King of Belgium. At about 12:00, he returned to the Cathay Hotel to rest. As for one of his daughters, she caught a cold during the trip and was sent to the hospital for treatment at about 3:00 in the afternoon and is expected to recover in a few days.

British Envoy Sir Odo (center) (Gong Shuxian Photo)

Releasing a Statement

At 8:40 yesterday morning, the British Envoy met with Chinese and foreign journalists in the hall on the ship and released a statement, saying: "I am deeply honored to be appointed as the Envoy to China. I received the order to make the mission last September, but I could not start the trip immediately due to some matters. It was not until today that I was able to arrive here safely. The friendly relations between China and Britain have always been very good. I will do my best in the future to seek ways to promote friendship between the two countries, so that the friendly relations between the two countries will be even better." After arriving in Shanghai today, I decided to take a short rest in Shanghai. I am scheduled to go to Beijing on March 2 to visit the National Government authorities. However, the date of presenting credentials will be determined after arriving in Beijing." The British Envoy then talked about the revision of the Sino-British Commercial Treaty, saying, "When I left the UK, I did not receive any instructions from the government regarding the revision of the Sino-British Commercial Treaty, so I have no opinion to express. I will carefully study this issue in the future so as to come up with a concrete plan to contribute to the government for adoption." As for the issue of moving the British Embassy to Beijing, in principle, the embassy should be in Beijing in order to facilitate contact. But in fact, it is necessary to consider all aspects."

Portuguese Envoy Returns Home This Afternoon

The Portuguese Envoy to China, Mr. Zhuba Weiya, has requested leave to return home. He arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing on the 24th of this month. After arriving in Shanghai, the Portuguese Envoy is scheduled to leave Shanghai by ship at about 1:00 this afternoon to return home. He will return to China in six months to cancel his leave.

National Government Advisor Frank Hinckley Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

Released a Written Statement

Mr. Frank Hinckley, the American advisor to the National Government, traveled around the world on the order of the National Government for talks, which lasted for eighteen months. Mr. Hinckley arrived in Shanghai yesterday on the Dollar Company's President Johnson and is scheduled to go to Beijing this Thursday (March 1) to report everything to the National Government authorities. The translated version of the written statement released by Mr. Hinckley in Shanghai is as follows:

"During my travels abroad, I met with many important political figures in Western countries. According to the representatives, they all trust the Nanjing National Government and are prepared to give it full assistance. They also feel that in order to promote the sale of their manufactured surplus products, they should also consult with the Nanjing National Government in order to have hope. In addition, I have had many contacts with business and industrial leaders in various countries, especially in the United States. The market situation in the United States is very bad at present, and many capitalists are willing to invest huge amounts of capital in China and seek to revitalize trade with China. They intend to obtain the credit of the Chinese side by adopting a new method of Sino-foreign cooperation. On the 15th of this month, I reported this matter to the National Government, but the content is too long to go into detail. If the issue of consular jurisdiction is resolved, American merchants can be tolerant of Chinese business habits in their dealings with Chinese companies and shops, so that they can trust each other. I am drafting two different plans to enable China to get rid of the shackles of unequal treaties as soon as possible in the spirit of mutual concessions. As soon as these two plans are drafted, they will be submitted to the National Government for research. Last summer, I traveled to Soviet Russia, and as a result, I felt more than ever that communism is absolutely incompatible with the national conditions of China. People of the world, except for the Communist Party, feel that Chinese culture is superior to other cultures. Unfortunately, the Chinese people have fallen into extreme poverty, and the reason for their poverty is mostly due to the foreign forces under the protection of unequal treaties. If unequal treaties continue to exist, the Communists will have an excuse to slander the National Government, thinking that the National Government condones foreigners to dominate China with unequal treaties as a talisman. May I ask whether there are any foreigners in China who are controlled by the Communist Party and are unwilling to reform the status quo according to reason? If not, why not unite with the general public, support the National Government, and cooperate with it? In this way, China can still be open to foreigners, and foreigners can make full use of China's large market and the goodwill of the Chinese people to promote international trade and international prosperity. Since October 1930, I have been working on the issue of the US government directly lending money to China. Regarding this matter, my colleagues in the United States and I have spent a great deal of effort and patience. The process has been written into a report and submitted to the National Government. No matter what the outcome of this matter is, it must be entirely attributed to the National Government, because the National Government has given correct guidance and constantly encouraged my work for Sino-US friendship. US President Roosevelt is, in my opinion, an ideal figure among Americans. His handwritten $50 million wheat loan to China will occupy an important page in Chinese history."

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Telegraphed the German Envoy to Make a Clear Statement on His Attitude Towards the Puppet Manchukuo

And Sent a Letter to the German Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai to Pay Attention

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce believes that Germany has recently had a proposal to recognize the puppet Manchukuo. According to reports, the country has denied the news, but there is no clear statement. Therefore, the German Envoy in Peiping was telegraphed to make a clear statement on his attitude towards the puppet Manchukuo, and the German Chamber of Commerce was also sent a letter to pay attention. The original text is recorded as follows:

Telegraph to the German Envoy

To His Excellency the German Envoy in Peiping: Cooperation between our two countries has made great progress in recent years. This kind of connection is completely built on the basis of your country's sympathy for China. In particular, your country's just attitude towards the case of the three northeastern provinces when it attended the League of Nations last year was praised by our country. However, there have been rumors in the international community recently, seeking to alienate the friendship between the two countries. It is believed that His Excellency is already familiar with them. In order to maintain the commercial future of the two countries, our association would like His Excellency to reaffirm your country's sympathy for China and its fair attitude, and to convey to your government the importance that our country's public opinion attaches to this issue. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce.

Letter to the German Chamber of Commerce

To the esteemed German Chamber of Commerce,

We begin by noting that cooperation between our two nations has seen significant progress recently. This situation is undoubtedly familiar to your esteemed Chamber and is a cause for mutual celebration for the future of both our countries. Our association believes the reason for this lies in the fact that both our nations find ourselves in the midst of difficult struggles. This naturally gives rise to a feeling of sympathy towards China. The impartial attitude your nation adopted towards the Manchurian Incident when attending the League of Nations last year sufficiently demonstrates the accuracy of our association's words. Unfortunately, there have been recent international rumors and telegrams implicating your nation. They claim that you will alter your previous policy regarding the Manchurian Incident. Although this is a form of propaganda stemming from a conspiracy, intending to sow discord between our two nations, a common saying in our country states, "No wind, no waves." Therefore, our association, for the sake of the future of both our nations, cannot but pay serious attention to this matter. We also hope that your esteemed Chamber, with its standing as a leader in the business community, can introduce the opinions of the people of our nation to your government. At the same time, this may also awaken your government to pay serious attention to this matter. This is addressed to the German Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai.

Shanghai Municipal Council Board of Directors Discusses Increasing Chinese Directors

Foreign Taxpayers Not Yet Able to Accept

At the Shanghai Municipal Council Board of Directors meeting on the 21st of this month, a letter from the Chinese Ratepayers' Association was presented. Based on the text and spirit of the documents exchanged when the Chinese Directorships were initially established in early 1928, it requested that the number of Chinese Directors be increased from five to nine within this year. The letter also expressed the hope that the number of Chinese Directors could be increased to match the proportion of Chinese tax contributions, so that Chinese and foreign residents could cooperate more closely and mutually benefit. After discussion, the Board of Directors expressed great sympathy for the wishes expressed by the Chinese residents in the letter. However, given that the election of Chinese Directors has only been in place for a short time, and in light of the prevailing public opinion among foreigners, the foreign directors felt that increasing the number was not appropriate at this time. Moreover, they were concerned that this proposal would be difficult to gain unanimous support from all the relevant nations. They decided to reply to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association with this sentiment. The request to increase the number of Chinese Directors is based on the proportion of tax contributions from Chinese and foreign citizens. According to the calculations of the Chinese Ratepayers' Association, this was 55 to 45 in 1928, and is now 64 to 36. However, the Board of Directors' discussion revealed that this calculation was based on a misunderstanding. In fact, in 1927, the amount of municipal general taxes paid by the Chinese accounted for 62 percent, while foreigners accounted for 38 percent, which is not much different from the current ratio of

Page 10

64 to 36. As for the ratio of 55 to 45 mentioned for 1928, it was the result of combining the four major revenue sources: municipal taxes, land taxes, license fees, and wharf dues. If calculated in the same way at this moment, the ratio would be approximately 57 to 43. If the amount of municipal fees provided by a certain group of residents is the sole basis for their number of representatives, there are many who oppose this view. As for the relationship between Chinese and foreign directors in recent years, it has been extremely harmonious. This is naturally due to the efforts of both sides to understand each other and express mutual sympathy. However, the foreign directors deeply feel that foreign taxpayers are not yet able to accept the idea of increasing the number of Chinese directors to the same number as foreign directors at this time.

Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau Promotes Factory Safety

Central News Agency reports that the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau, in order to promote factory safety in the city and to understand the actual conditions of each factory, had planned to engage in factory inspections and factory surveys. However, the factory inspection has been hindered by the authorities of the concessions and has not been able to proceed. The factory survey has already been completed. Details of the situation are as follows:

Factory Inspection

According to a spokesperson for the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau, factory inspections have been difficult to carry out even in the city due to obstruction from the concession authorities. However, given the importance of factory safety equipment, a solution should be sought quickly. Our authorities are planning to break the deadlock within the next two months and prevent this situation from continuing indefinitely. Before Director Li Pingheng of the Ministry of Industry travels abroad to attend the International Labour Conference, if there is still no practical solution, this case will be brought before the International Labour Conference to seek a fair decision. Currently, the Ministry of Industry is still working hard on factory inspections. Cities such as Qingdao and Hangzhou have already started to implement them. Recently, the Ministry of Industry will also conduct factory inspections in Wuxi, as Wuxi is an important industrial area with numerous factories. The work of inspecting factories should be urgently planned and implemented. It is likely that the authorities of this city will be consulted again at an appropriate time to carry out the work of inspecting factories in Shanghai.

Detailed Investigation of Factory Conditions

Although the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau cannot currently carry out factory inspections, it has conducted a detailed investigation of the actual conditions of each factory. This will be done annually in the future. The information collected last year has been compiled into a "Directory of Shanghai Factories for the 22nd Year", which is expected to be finalized and published in the near future. After the publication of this directory, the investigation into the actual conditions of each factory in this city this year will continue.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Pays Attention to Industrial and Commercial Laws and Regulations

Submitting a Request for Each Law and Regulation to be Studied Before it is Put to a Vote

The Chamber Can Provide Answers for Various Industries if They Encounter Difficulties

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce believes that industrial and commercial laws and regulations are of great importance to the interests of each industry, and has therefore established an Industrial and Commercial Laws and Regulations Research Committee to conduct research. It is learned that the Chamber yesterday submitted a request to the Legislative Yuan, requesting that the draft of each law and regulation be submitted to the Chamber for research before it is put to a vote. At the same time, it notified each industry that if they encounter any difficulties with laws and regulations, they should notify the Chamber in writing so that it can conduct research on their behalf. The letter of submission is recorded as follows:

Submission to the Legislative Yuan

Submission Regarding a Request, It has been found that since the establishment of your esteemed Yuan, various industrial and commercial laws and regulations in our country have been successively formulated, and there are already many types. However, the purpose of legislation should not only advance with the trends of the world, but also seek to be in line with national conditions. The area where our association is located is the center of our country's commercial market, and the soundness of the formulation of laws is deeply and greatly related to the prosperity and decline of industry and commerce. Therefore, since last year, we have established an Industrial and Commercial Laws and Regulations Research Committee, inviting experts and giants from various industries to engage in the research of industrial and commercial laws and regulations. We have learned that when your esteemed Yuan formulates the Constitution, it first discloses the initial draft in the newspapers for criticism from all walks of life as a step towards accepting amendments. This is a display of impartiality that we deeply admire. Although industrial and commercial laws and regulations cannot be compared to the fundamental laws of the country, they cannot be ignored from the point of view of their relationship to the national economy and the people's livelihood. Therefore, we venture to submit this document to your esteemed Yuan for review and approval. Hereafter, when drafting industrial and commercial laws and regulations, we humbly request that the original draft be issued to our association for research before it is put to a vote, so that we can do our best to contribute our sincerity and assist your esteemed Yuan. We deeply implore this.

Letter to Various Associations

Esteemed Sirs, At the 65th Standing Committee meeting of the association held on the 22nd of this month, the meeting resolutions of the Industrial and Commercial Laws and Regulations Research Committee of the association were discussed, proposing to send a circular to various industry associations and store members, stating that if they encounter any difficulties regarding industrial and commercial laws and regulations in the future, they can report them in writing, so that we can research and reply. The matter has been discussed and approved on record. Correspondingly, we send a circular to notify you, hoping that you will take note. In the future, if any difficult problems arise regarding the Wang Commercial Law and Regulations, you can notify the association in writing at any time, so that we can forward them for research and reply.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Writes to the Stamp Tax Bureau to Discuss Stamp Inspection Methods

Personnel from Branch Offices Will Accompany in Wusong and Other Places

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday wrote to the Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau to discuss stamp inspection methods. The original letter is recorded as follows: Esteemed Sirs, It has been found that your bureau's inspection of whether stamp taxes have been omitted or not, according to your authority, is carried out at any time, originally for the purpose of benefiting tax revenue. However, the situation in each rural town is different. If a thorough, cautious, and careful method can be properly planned, it can be handled in your bureau, which can reduce misunderstandings, and inland stores can be spared unnecessary suspicion. Therefore, our association proposes three matters to your bureau: (1) Our association has branch offices in Wusong, Jiangwan, and Pudong. We propose that when stamp inspections are carried out in these three places, the branch offices should be notified to appoint personnel to accompany them. (2) A receipt should be issued to the inspected store for any violations found. (3) For various account books and documents, the inspector should instruct the store clerk to open the cabinets themselves and take out the items for inspection. The above three points do not harm public affairs and are beneficial to commercial sentiment. Your bureau has always been accommodating to commercial sentiment and should be able to grant our request. Accordingly, this letter is sent to request your consideration and reply.

Ministry of Communications Investigates and Confiscates Private Official and Military Telegrams

To be Implemented Starting Tomorrow

The Shanghai Telegraph Bureau yesterday received instructions from the Ministry of Communications, stating that the use of official and military stationery to send private military telegrams has been repeatedly ordered by the Ministry to be investigated and confiscated by the bureaus. However, recently, the number of these private official and military telegrams has increased again, not only affecting telegraph revenue, but also congesting lines, causing delays in important telegrams. If strict measures are not taken, the harm will be great. In order to effectively rectify the situation, the Ministry has once again revised the measures for investigating and confiscating private official and military telegrams as follows: (1) Private official and military telegrams should be detained by the sending, receiving, and relaying bureaus in accordance with regulations. (2) All congratulatory telegrams sent by party, government, and military agencies using official stationery, except for telegrams sent to the central government to celebrate national events, which should be classified as first-class telegrams, shall be charged as social telegrams. (3) All coded telegrams sent by government and military personnel to other government and military personnel or private individuals using official stationery must be confirmed to be sent on official business. If it is found to be private business, fees shall be charged in accordance with regulations. (4) If the personnel of the sending and receiving bureaus fail to detain private official and military telegrams that pass through them, once discovered, each shall be fined two cents per word. (5) If the sending bureau does not detain private official and military telegrams and is detained by the receiving bureau, in addition to the sending bureau personnel being fined two cents per word as stipulated above, the receiving bureau personnel shall be awarded two cents per word. (6) The original copies of outgoing telegrams or copies of incoming telegrams of private official and military telegrams detained by the sending or receiving bureaus shall be submitted to the Ministry for verification on a monthly basis. (7) When the receiving bureau detains private official and military telegrams, there is no need to notify the sending bureau with an official telegram. The recipient should be charged for the service and delivery of the telegram, and the copy of the telegram should still be submitted for verification. (8) These measures will be implemented starting March 1, 1934. The above measures, in addition to being submitted to the Executive Yuan, have also been communicated to the Military Commission and the Ministry of Military Administration to be notified to all telegraph personnel for investigation and compliance. It is hereby ordered that the bureau shall comply with these measures to maintain telegraph administration.

Since the 19th Route Army was reorganized by the Central Government, more than 600 sick and wounded soldiers have been recovered. Those who recovered from illness have also joined the Central Army on their own initiative, leaving a net total of more than 1,900 people. Among them, 1,530 were from Guangdong and Guangxi. The Fujian Provincial Government gave each person 2 yuan, and the Fujian Red Cross Branch chartered the Xinming Steamboat to send them back to Guangzhou. Removal of Shallow Water Fee in North China

Original Status Restored on March 1st

China Merchants Bureau North China Ships Resume Service

Every winter, due to difficult navigation on the icy river, shipping companies in North China typically increase shallow water freight rates by 20% starting December 1st. Now, as the weather warms and the Baihe River is navigable without obstruction, the Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, and China Merchants Steam Navigation Company have agreed to cancel the shallow water fee for the icy river period, effective March 1st. Additionally, the China Merchants Bureau's North China liners, "Xinfeng" and "Xinming," suspended service after the Fujian Incident and were dedicated to official duties. Now that the remnants of the 19th Route Army from Fuzhou have been transported to Pukou and transferred to Henan for reorganization, a third batch of over 10,000 soldiers has been loaded onto Nanjing shipping vessels. The "Xinfeng" has already been sent back to Shanghai. The China Merchants Bureau has decided to resume the North China route with the "Xinfeng" starting March 1st.
